## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws & integrated concentration–time dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, so the task is to discover an ODE rate law for a chemical reaction system. With only (t, A) available, the most likely models are single-species kinetic laws (zero/first/second/nth order), possible reversible relaxation to equilibrium, or empirical time-dependent forcing/deactivation expressed directly as functions of t and A.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/production when supply or surface sites saturate)
- Time-varying zero-order term: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or reagent feed that decays in time)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, pseudo-first-order conditions)
- First-order with baseline/source: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant feed with first-order removal; CSTR-like linear kinetics)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or 2A -> products)
- General power-law (nth-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical rate order from data)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible autocatalysis (logistic-type in A): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalytic growth with depletion/finite capacity)
- Inhibited/limited-rate form: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate increases with A but becomes limited at high A due to inhibition/active-site limitation)
- Substrate activation with offset: dA_dt = -c0 * (A + c1)**c2 (effective concentration shifted by background/measurement offset or competing pool)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (deactivation/temperature ramp proxy): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (first-order with exponentially decaying activity)
- Piecewise effective first-order (induction time): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) (slow activation/induction then standard decay)
- Empirical non-separable law: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t + c2 * t**2) * A (time-polynomial effective rate constant capturing external program)
- Stretched-exponential / distributed kinetics proxy: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (effective rate grows or decays as a power of time, mimicking aging or changing environment)
- Oscillatory forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodic modulation of rate via mixing/light/temperature cycling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over A, favor zero-order forms (dA_dt ≈ -c0) and expect A vs t to be roughly linear until depletion.
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (dA_dt/A ≈ constant), favor first-order; plotting log(A) vs t should be near-linear in the noise-free ideal case.
- If dA_dt scales like A**2 (dA_dt/A**2 ≈ constant), favor second-order; 1/A vs t tends to be near-linear for clean second-order decay.
- If the apparent rate constant changes with time (dA_dt/A varies systematically with t), model k(t) via exp(-c*t), t**c, or low-order polynomials multiplying A.
- If A tends toward a nonzero plateau where dA_dt → 0, include an equilibrium/offset term like (A - c1) or c0 - c1*A.
- If the magnitude of dA_dt rises at early times then later falls without external forcing, consider autocatalytic structure A*(c - A) or A*(A - c) depending on sign.
- If dA_dt increases with A at low A but levels off at high A, use a rational limitation such as A/(A + c) to represent active-site limitation or inhibition.
- If there is an induction period (near-zero dA_dt at small t) followed by normal kinetics, multiply by an activation factor like (1 - exp(-c*t)).
- If the sign of dA_dt flips (net production then net consumption), consider source–sink competition c0 - c1*A or time-dependent forcing terms added to a decay law.
- If periodic structure appears in residuals versus t, incorporate sinusoidal modulation of an effective rate coefficient multiplying A.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK0)

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.18997742423620262*A**2 + 0.45987487478174419*A**2/(0.7497988950401423*A**4 + 1)`

Let me simplify the GT. The second term can be rewritten:
`0.45987487478174419*A**2/(0.7497988950401423*A**4 + 1)`

So GT = `-c0*A^2 + c2*A^2/(c4*A^4 + 1)` which is a rational function in A with no dependence on t.

The GT is a function of A only (not t). Let me analyze the structure:
- It has a polynomial term `-0.19*A^2`
- Plus a rational term `~0.46*A^2/(0.75*A^4 + 1)`

For large A, the rational term → 0.46/(0.75*A^2) → 0, so GT ~ -0.19*A^2.
For small A, GT ~ -0.19*A^2 + 0.46*A^2 = 0.27*A^2.

The GT can be written as a single rational expression:
`(-0.19*A^2*(0.75*A^4 + 1) + 0.46*A^2) / (0.75*A^4 + 1)`
= `(-0.1425*A^6 - 0.19*A^2 + 0.46*A^2) / (0.75*A^4 + 1)`
= `(-0.1425*A^6 + 0.27*A^2) / (0.75*A^4 + 1)`

So GT = `A^2*(-0.1425*A^4 + 0.27) / (0.75*A^4 + 1)`

This is a rational function of A. The key structural features:
- It's a ratio of a degree-6 polynomial over a degree-4 polynomial (in A)
- No t dependence
- No transcendental functions (sin, exp, log, sqrt)

Now let me check each candidate for structural compatibility:

**Candidates with transcendental functions (sin, exp, log, tanh, sqrt) that cannot be eliminated:**

Candidates 1-5, 7, 11-14, 16-19, 21-28, 30, 32, 34, 36-72, 74-77 all contain transcendental functions (exp, sin, log, sqrt, tanh) or fractional powers. For these to match, ALL transcendental/irrational terms must be eliminable by setting coefficients to 0.

Let me focus on candidates that could potentially be pure rational functions of A:

**Candidate 6:** `A^3*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c3*exp(A*c4) + c5/A + c6/A^3`
Set c3=0: `A^3*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c5/A + c6/A^3` - this is a Laurent polynomial, not a rational function with denominator `0.75*A^4+1`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1 + A*c2 + A*c3/(A*c4 + c5) + c6 + c7/(A*c4 + c5) + c8/A + c9/A^3`
Combining over common denominator `A^3*(A*c4+c5)`: This has denominator linear in A (times A^3), but GT needs degree-4 denominator. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 9:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1 + A*c2 + c3 + c4/(A*c5 + c6) + c7/A + c8/A^3`
Similar issue - denominator is linear. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1 + A*c2 + A^c3*c4 + c5 + c6/A + c7/A^3`
Set c3=2: `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1 + A*c2 + c4*A^2 + c5 + c6/A + c7/A^3` - polynomial/Laurent, not rational. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 73:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1 + A*c2 + c3 + c4/A + c5/A^2 + c6/A^3` - Laurent polynomial. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 15, 20:** Contain t-dependence that can be zeroed. After zeroing t terms, same as Candidate 9 structure. [NO MATCH]

After careful analysis, none of the candidates can produce the rational function structure `A^2/(c*A^4+1)` that appears in the GT. The GT requires a quartic polynomial denominator, which none of these candidates provide.

Matched candidate IDs: []

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match
